  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_84ee6566-e420-4874-8bc1-ff5dc46f9d8b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer15038517323149252671"><b>THE REVIEW</b><br/><br/><b>Why this book?</b><br/><br/>I love this series<br/><br/><b>What I thought</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469124293ra/19783705.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>OMG this was amazing !!! It was full of action, adventure,LMAO moments and new memorable characters. Along with the characters we all know and love. At first when I heard they were going into Connors stories I was disappointed but I was so wrong Connors stories were awesome. I just loved how Conner and Alex's mom and step dad and the fairytale characters had to babysit Connors characters. That whole situation was just hilarious. Oh and Trol</span>
  <span id="freeText15038517323149252671" style="display:none"><b>THE REVIEW</b><br><br><b>Why this book?</b><br><br>I love this series<br><br><b>What I thought</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469124293ra/19783705.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>OMG this was amazing !!! It was full of action, adventure,LMAO moments and new memorable characters. Along with the characters we all know and love. At first when I heard they were going into Connors stories I was disappointed but I was so wrong Connors stories were awesome. I just loved how Conner and Alex's mom and step dad and the fairytale characters had to babysit Connors characters. That whole situation was just hilarious. Oh and Trollbellas Play = Priceless . I also loved seeing what was happening in the fairytale world even though most of the key players were gone. As for the cliffhanger OMG can't wait till the next book!!! Thankfully this wasn't the last book, because I wasn't ready to say goodbye.</span>

  <span id="freeText200404621054742642" style="display:none">So I just finished this book. It was awesome except for the ending... Watching Alex and Connor grow up and growing up with them is a great gift. You won't want to put this series down. Like, ever.<br /><br />The cliffhangers left me basically crying but it's worth it. <br />To everyone: READ THIS SERIES!! It is so creative and witty and just on my scale of zero to rainbow unicorns it is definitely a rainbow unicorn. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1178795312" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1178795312" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33012180-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537582300p2/33012180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1178795312?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/33012180-chelsea">Chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33012180-chelsea?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1178795312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6692154635253711837">I wouldn’t trust my rating for this book. <b>I’m honestly not sure if this series has actually decreased in quality, or I have just outgrown them, all I know is that I didn’t enjoy this one like I enjoyed the rest of the books.</b><br/><br/>To be fair, I was having a lot of trouble remembering what happened in the previous book. I really just can’t wait a year in between books; I forget everything!<br/><br/><b>I remember really enjoying the first three books. They were funny, had a great premise, and felt magical. I just did</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6692154635253711837" style="display:none">I wouldn’t trust my rating for this book. <b>I’m honestly not sure if this series has actually decreased in quality, or I have just outgrown them, all I know is that I didn’t enjoy this one like I enjoyed the rest of the books.</b><br /><br />To be fair, I was having a lot of trouble remembering what happened in the previous book. I really just can’t wait a year in between books; I forget everything!<br /><br /><b>I remember really enjoying the first three books. They were funny, had a great premise, and felt magical. I just didn’t feel that way with the last two, especially this one.</b> Maybe it is because I’m getting older and have outgrown books with such a young and silly tone, but I could pinpoint a lot of issues, so I do think that this one was the weakest one.<br /><br />This one mostly follows Conner and Alex as they venture into Conner’s stories in order to recruit his characters to help them in fairytale world.<br /><br />I’m pretty sure it’s every writer’s dream to go hang out in the world they created with their characters, but this plot felt like complete filler. <b>It felt so dragged out, and I honestly didn’t care about Conner’s characters. We already had an established cast of characters from the first four books, we didn’t need a bunch of new ones.<br /><br />That’s one of the big problems with this one; too many characters.</b> Omg, there are SO many! Like why do we need to see from the point of view of the Book Huggers? What even is that random plotline? I like seeing a lot of perspectives, but when you have that many characters it becomes hard to be invested in any of them.<br /><br />This book is also ridiculously long. There are some books that can be over 400 pages and that’s the right length, but this isn’t one of them. <b>So much of this book is made up of unnecessary filler and set up, which made me have an overall tedious reading experience where I was just waiting for it to be done.</b><br /><br />There are interesting bits, like back in fairytale world. It was hard for me to care though, because the The Masked Man is a cartoonishly evil and one dimensional villain.<br /><br /><b>Pretty sure I’ve pointed this out in my review for each book in the series but THE ITALICIZING! Omg, I have <i>never</i>, in all the books I have ever read, seen someone so obsessed with the italics button.</b> Like, it’s becoming harder and harder for me to deal with. It’s just bad writing.<br /><br />I’m assuming (and hoping) that the next book is the last. I will be reading it, because I like the main characters and have already spent my time reading five books in this series, but I don’t think I would recommend them at this point.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6692154635253711837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4038922559605895391" style="display:none">DNF <br /><br />Mini review:<br /><br />I have thoroughly enjoyed the previous books in this series. It was also funny and comical, especially with one of Conner's typos (rosary chicken instead of rotisserie chicken). </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7248964396547104322">I absolutely loved the first two books in this series, unfortunately, I have liked the later books less and less. I was completely intrigued by this one as they go into Conner's stories, but it didn't do much for me. What was so spectacular about the first two books was looking at the fairy tale world in a completely different light. The books have lost that magic. There are still moments of brilliance and insight, but over-all, it didn't wow me. I'm mailing this out to my daughter at sleep-away</span>
  <span id="freeText7248964396547104322" style="display:none">I absolutely loved the first two books in this series, unfortunately, I have liked the later books less and less. I was completely intrigued by this one as they go into Conner's stories, but it didn't do much for me. What was so spectacular about the first two books was looking at the fairy tale world in a completely different light. The books have lost that magic. There are still moments of brilliance and insight, but over-all, it didn't wow me. I'm mailing this out to my daughter at sleep-away camp tomorrow and she will probably completely disagree with me.</span>

I just wish that Mr. Colfer provided a reason for Alex and Conner to be unable to simply write "There was an army that could defeat the Literary Army that waited for Alex and Conner to command them" and then take this army to Land of Stories.   <span id="freeText14380435573563841973" style="display:none">Review below is mostly accurate. I just wish that Mr. Colfer provided a reason for Alex and Conner to be unable to simply write "There was an army that could defeat the Literary Army that waited for Alex and Conner to command them" and then take this army to Land of Stories. I understand that actually doing that would obviously make for a short book, but I just wish there was an explanation against it. <br />******************************<br />Read this in one sitting and was at the edge of my seat the whole time. Thank god the Masked Man is gone. He was getting annoying and the witches and literary villains are a much more menacing antagonist. He had a very fitting ending.<br />All the plotlines, Grimm, Himmelsbach, Witches, Twins, are converging. I think that the last chapter with the President could have been done better. The plan with the dust draws from an old fairy tale not well-known. so kudos to Chris for using it. <br />Charlotte had some great scenes in the book that showed her as a character not just their absentee mother. <br />Next book is going to have lots of sudden meetings allowing all the groups to work together because that army is now going to have to fight witches, not the masked man's army though they will also have to do that to free the fairy tale world. I hope that it doesn't lead to a double world thing where regular people travel back and forth and the worlds are symbiotically together. <br />Read for Booktubeathon challenge to read a book by a favorite author</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tarmia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tarmia" href="/user/show/46015060-tarmia">Tarmia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46015060-tarmia?shelf=adolescent-fiction">adolescent-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46015060-tarmia?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46015060-tarmia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1725833651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8456621738650592474">This is the second to last installment in The Land of Stories series and was a welcomed installment at that. Colfer has a great ability to continue to create original and fun adventures even while using the recycled idea of fairy tale characters. <br/>The added enjoyment of the main boy, Connor's, original characters from his own stories is really well done and Colfer is able to blend classic and new characters together without creating an awkward divide. He uses it to its best comic ability. This wo</span>
  <span id="freeText8456621738650592474" style="display:none">This is the second to last installment in The Land of Stories series and was a welcomed installment at that. Colfer has a great ability to continue to create original and fun adventures even while using the recycled idea of fairy tale characters. <br />The added enjoyment of the main boy, Connor's, original characters from his own stories is really well done and Colfer is able to blend classic and new characters together without creating an awkward divide. He uses it to its best comic ability. This works very well. I am quite a big fan of middle-grade fiction, I like its freedom and imagination as well as how anything can happen. There seem to be far fewer rules for middle-grade fiction. I really look forward to the last book and definitely recommend this to anyone looking for a series to just enjoy and have fun with while reading. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8456621738650592474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2215264814" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2215264814" />
    <a title="Meg McGregor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5554878-meg-mcgregor"><img alt="Meg McGregor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598205428p2/5554878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2215264814?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meg McGregor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meg McGregor" href="/user/show/5554878-meg-mcgregor">Meg McGregor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5554878-meg-mcgregor?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5554878-meg-mcgregor?shelf=series-i-love">series-i-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2215264814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14970520708104752566">I think it is only fitting that the last book I read and review in 2017 is this fantastic book about stories!<br/><br/>This is such a wonderful series and I will really be sad when I have finished it, after I read the next book, the conclusion of the saga!<br/><br/>A quote that sums up this series to me, is as follows!<br/><br/>"With that said, I have a favor to ask of anyone reading this: Become a storyteller! Read to others the fairy tales in this book. Read them stories from another book. If you can, create your own stori</span>
  <span id="freeText14970520708104752566" style="display:none">I think it is only fitting that the last book I read and review in 2017 is this fantastic book about stories!<br /><br />This is such a wonderful series and I will really be sad when I have finished it, after I read the next book, the conclusion of the saga!<br /><br />A quote that sums up this series to me, is as follows!<br /><br />"With that said, I have a favor to ask of anyone reading this: Become a storyteller! Read to others the fairy tales in this book. Read them stories from another book. If you can, create your own stories to share. When you pass along the art of storytelling to your family and friends, you make the world a better place."<br /><br />Children are not being read these stories right now. They are instead introduced to video games and violence at the age they should be exploring witches and high towers, giants and Thumbelina, Fairy Godmothers and pumpkins. Magic has indeed lost its way in our world but I believe that we can still get it back!<br /><br />Thanks Mr. Colfer for writing this series! It is a remarkable achievement.<br /><br />I have written a children's book about the special relationship between a raggedy old bear named Sad Eyes and my daughter when she was three years old. I have thought about submitting it but am just too afraid. Maybe one day I will find the courage I need to let my story out into the world.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1330321622" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1330321622" />
    <a title="Thibaut Nicodème" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22674620-thibaut-nicod-me"><img alt="Thibaut Nicodème" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574079623p2/22674620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1330321622?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thibaut Nicodème" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thibaut Nicodème" href="/user/show/22674620-thibaut-nicod-me">Thibaut Nicodème</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1330321622" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12907715853717677491">So…the usual first: I still really like Chris Colfer's writing. Well, specifically I like things about his writing that make the rest palatable. Yeah, his turns of phrase could use improvement (and especially variety), but the story behind it is pretty good and I am 100% in love with <s>him</s> his sense of humor.<br/><br/>This book builds up on the previous one's story (and <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ending once more on a cliffhanger, which…I'm not sure how I feel about, to be entirely honest <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>). Instead of c</span>
  <span id="freeText12907715853717677491" style="display:none">So…the usual first: I still really like Chris Colfer's writing. Well, specifically I like things about his writing that make the rest palatable. Yeah, his turns of phrase could use improvement (and especially variety), but the story behind it is pretty good and I am 100% in love with <s>him</s> his sense of humor.<br /><br />This book builds up on the previous one's story (and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ending once more on a cliffhanger, which…I'm not sure how I feel about, to be entirely honest <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>). Instead of classic literary worlds, we visit…"original" ones by Conner Bailey. Which are basically AU fanfic of his friends and/or himself.<br /><br />Yeah, this is where we get into "why I give this book 4 stars instead of 5". Well, the main reason why. See, this book seems to imply "write what you know" is literally the <i>only</i> way to write. Which I hate. Hell, I'm not even comfortable with the idea that every story an author writes has to be inherently personal. I could probably write a whole essay on the matter, because I have very strong feelings, but this is not the time nor the place.<br /><br />Then it kind of flip-flops on the author's relationship with his characters, going so far as to imply writers' imagination are merely a gateway into another world and Conner didn't <i>create</i> his characters, but the first story we see is influenced by typos Conner wrote, which implies he did in fact influence them? It's all very confused as a result.<br /><br />That part gets even worse in the climax, where…<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Bree's story is brought to life and includes an undead Bo Peep, who apparently has all the memories of the real Bo Peep. Does that mean all these worlds are connected somehow? Is this Bo Peep just a clone, so to speak? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Oh, speaking of the climax, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the Masked Man <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> dying feel a bit like a weird copout, considering how <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was set up as the biggest threat around.<br /><br />The other reason I took a star off? The…weird race shit. I know the stories are meant to be the work of a pre-teen/young teenager, but when the one character who's established as a black man is also the scaryevil pirate, it…raises concerns. And then we have the frankly insulting treatment of India and Egypt later on (and by the way, they fly from one to the other overnight when the information I get online tells me a blimp would take 4-5 days to make the trip), which is just…I get that Conner is probably ignorant of all that stuff, but did you have to base one of the four main set pieces in your book around that ignorance?<br /><br />(Also, a pharaoh would totally be buried with a mummified cat, not a dog. The cat person in me is offended by that part)<br /><br />Anyway. The book's still really good, and you know I just love bitching. Besides, if you're interesting in reading a review for book 5 in a series, you're probably going to read it anyway, so it's not like my opinion on this will sway you one war or the other.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12907715853717677491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tN1JbeC13Vr6A6a1CivLJl3SWPux6Y9+PMv0WLhiE5ePmRfIHB0tLJxGhBjJzMyjel6f09jbAT6nNkwegA/CPQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }
